## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of population change (dP/dt) as a function of time and population size, which is the central problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from exponential growth to density-dependent and time-varying models.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, no density dependence)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + c2)) (growth slowing logarithmically near carrying capacity)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Strong Allee cubic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - P) * (P - c2) (bistable population dynamics)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent with hyperbolic saturation)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * (c3 + c4 * P) (flexible asymmetric growth curve)
- Time-dependent Malthusian: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponential growth with time-varying rate)
- Seasonal/periodic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (oscillatory environmental forcing)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional/anomalous growth kinetics)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent growth minus proportional removal)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Time-modulated logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * t) (logistic with linearly changing environment)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Quadratic dependence on P (P*(1-P/K) form) → logistic-type density regulation with a single stable equilibrium at carrying capacity
- Cubic dependence on P (P*(P-a)*(K-P) form) → Allee effect with bistability and a critical population threshold
- Logarithmic coupling log(K/P) multiplied by P → Gompertz-type growth with asymmetric approach to carrying capacity (slower near K)
- Rational form P/(1+cP) → contest competition where per-capita resources saturate hyperbolically with density
- Multiplicative time-periodic modulation sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) on growth rate → seasonal or circadian environmental forcing
- Difference of power laws (P^a - P^b with a<b) → metabolic scaling models balancing anabolic and catabolic processes
- Exponential decay in time multiplying growth rate exp(-c*t) → resource depletion or environmental degradation over time
- Product of multiple linear factors in P → multiple equilibria corresponding to roots, with stability alternating between them
- Square root or fractional power P^(2/3) or P^(3/4) → surface-area-to-volume scaling in metabolic growth theories

$$f(t,P) = 0.1728(1 - P/48.55)P + \frac{0.1728 \cdot P}{1 + \exp(-1.524(-0.924 + P))}$$

Let me simplify the GT:
$$f = 0.1728P - 0.003558P^2 + \frac{0.1728P}{1 + \exp(-1.524P + 1.408)}$$

The key structure is: **quadratic in P** (specifically $aP^2 + bP$) plus a **sigmoid-like term** $\frac{cP}{1+\exp(-dP+e)}$.

Now, I need to check if `P/(1+exp(-αP+β))` can be expressed using `tanh`. Recall:
$$\frac{1}{1+e^{-x}} = \frac{1}{2}(1 + \tanh(x/2))$$

So: $\frac{cP}{1+\exp(-\alpha P + \beta)} = \frac{cP}{2}(1 + \tanh(\frac{\alpha P - \beta}{2}))$
$= \frac{cP}{2} + \frac{cP}{2}\tanh(\frac{\alpha P - \beta}{2})$

This gives us: $\frac{c}{2}P\cdot\tanh(\frac{\alpha}{2}P - \frac{\beta}{2}) + \frac{c}{2}P$

So the GT becomes:
$$f = aP^2 + bP + \frac{c}{2}P + \frac{c}{2}P\cdot\tanh\left(\frac{\alpha}{2}P - \frac{\beta}{2}\right)$$
$$= aP^2 + (b + c/2)P + \frac{c}{2}P\cdot\tanh\left(\frac{\alpha}{2}P - \frac{\beta}{2}\right)$$

This has the form: $P^2 \cdot c_0 + P \cdot c_1 + P \cdot c_2 \cdot \tanh(P \cdot c_3 + c_4)$

This is exactly **Candidate 24**: `P**2*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*tanh(P*c3 + c4)`

Let me verify with specific values:
- $a = -0.003558$ → $c_0 = -0.003558$
- $c/2 = 0.1728/2 = 0.0864$ → $c_2 = 0.0864$
- $\alpha/2 = 1.524/2 = 0.762$ → $c_3 = 0.762$
- $-\beta/2 = -1.408/2 = -0.704$ → $c_4 = -0.704$
- $b + c/2 = 0.1728 + 0.0864 = 0.2592$ → $c_1 = 0.2592$

This works perfectly. The GT is independent of $t$, and Candidate 24 is also independent of $t$.
